● Searched for 3 patterns (ctrl+o to expand)

● Found it. The problem is on line 159 — "message": json.dumps(payload). The entire event dict is being JSON-stringified
   and crammed into the message field. So the build log shows raw JSON like {"event_type": "bee_exec... instead of a
  human-readable message.

  Let me see how the build monitor picks up this message to display it.

● Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● The issue is clear. Line 159: "message": json.dumps(payload) dumps the entire raw JSON dict as the message. The build
  monitor's _is_state_transition then treats this as a new message and logs it to the build log, where it shows up as
  raw JSON.

  The fix: generate a human-readable summary instead of dumping the whole payload.

> only 24 tasks in 16 hours????

● You're right — that's slow. 15 actually delivered code, 4 were just Q33N writing task files (coordination overhead),
  and 5 never even got dispatched. The bees that ran completed clean, but the pipeline throughput is the problem.

  The bottlenecks I can see:

  1. Q33NR → Q33N → review → approve → dispatch is too many serial handoffs before a single bee even starts
  2. 5 tasks never started — task files sat there with nobody dispatching them
  3. Coordination-only tasks (231, 240, 241) — Q33N wrote task files and stopped, waiting for approval that never came
  because nobody was watching
  4. Single-threaded dispatch — bees ran one or two at a time instead of 5 parallel

  For a 16-hour window with parallel dispatch, this should have been 40-60 completed tasks, not 15.

  What do you want to do about it? Options:

  - Blast the undispatched backlog now — I can send Q33N to dispatch all 9 waiting tasks in parallel immediately
  - Tighten the pipeline — give Q33N standing approval to dispatch without waiting for Q33NR review (faster but less
  oversight)
  - Both — blast now + change the process for future runs

> 1 that bottlenext is NECESSARY to prevent errors in delivery. if a damn Claude Agent could actually get shit
  right the first time, we wouldnt need it.

● Fair point. The audit just proved it — two Haiku bees skipped the mandatory 8-section response file, one blew past the
   500-line limit. Without the review chain those errors ship unchecked. The pipeline isn't the problem.

  The real throughput loss is:
  - 5 tasks sitting there never dispatched — nobody was watching
  - Gaps between dispatch cycles — bee finishes, response sits for hours before Q33N picks it up
  - Q33N stopping to wait instead of dispatching everything it has approval for in parallel

  The chain of command is right. The cadence is wrong. Want me to blast the 9 undispatched tasks out now?

● Let me check what's actually documented in the processes.

● Searched for 1 pattern, read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

● Here's what I found:

  What IS documented:
  - P-03 says "Parallel when tasks are independent. Sequential when dependent." and HIVE.md Step 6 says "Never more than
   5 bees in parallel"
  - P-14 has the queue runner with --watch mode and Fibonacci backoff polling
  - Bee watchdog handles stale bees (8-min timeout, auto-restart)

  What is NOT documented — the gaps:

  1. No dispatch cadence rule for Q33N. HIVE.md Step 6 says "dispatch bees" but nothing about what Q33N does after
  dispatching. It just... stops. There's no rule saying "monitor running bees and dispatch the next batch as slots free
  up."
  2. No completion pickup rule. When a bee finishes and writes a response file, there's no documented trigger for Q33N
  to pick it up. Right now it requires Q33NR to manually dispatch another Q33N session to review results. That's the
  hours-long gap.
  3. Parallel dispatch is mentioned but not enforced. "Parallel when independent" is soft language. There's no rule
  saying "ALWAYS fill all 5 slots. If you have 8 independent tasks and 5 slots, dispatch 5 immediately, then backfill as
   slots clear."
  4. No standing orders for Q33N between dispatch cycles. Q33N is fire-and-forget — it runs, does one thing, exits.
  There's no "stay alive and manage the full batch lifecycle" instruction.

  So the answer is: the rules exist in pieces but nobody wrote the glue. The queue runner (run_queue.py --watch) was
  built to solve this for automated dispatch, but Q33N's manual coordination workflow has no equivalent.

  Want me to draft process updates to close these gaps?

╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌╌
 Plan: Q33N Dispatch Lifecycle & Parallel Slot Rules

 Context

 The audit revealed that only 15 tasks completed in 16 hours because:
 - Q33N dispatches bees and then exits. Nobody monitors completion.
 - A separate Q33N session has to be spun up later to review results — hours-long gaps.
 - Parallel slots aren't being maximized.
 - No documented rule telling Q33N to stay alive and manage the full batch.

 The review chain (Q33NR -> Q33N -> review -> approve -> dispatch) is NECESSARY and stays. What changes is Q33N's
 behavior AFTER dispatch approval.

 Changes

 1. Rewrite HIVE.md Q33N Steps 6-8

 File: .deia/HIVE.md (lines 174-202)

 Replace the current Steps 6-8 with a new lifecycle that covers:

 Step 6: Dispatch bees (fill all slots).
 - Dispatch ALL independent tasks in parallel up to the slot limit (5 peak / 10 off-peak per queue.yml).
 - Do not dispatch 1 or 2 when you have 8 independent tasks and 5 open slots. Fill every slot.
 - Dependent tasks queue behind their blockers.

 Step 7: Monitor and review (stay alive).
 - After dispatching, DO NOT EXIT. Stay alive and poll for completion.
 - Check .deia/hive/responses/ for new response files matching your dispatched task IDs.
 - Poll every 60 seconds. Do not spin (no sub-second loops). Do not sleep for minutes.
 - When a response file appears, immediately review it:
   - All 8 sections present? Tests pass? No stubs? No regressions?
   - If PASS: mark task as verified, write to completion report.
   - If FAIL: write a fix task and dispatch it into the freed slot (backfill).
 - The Q33N that dispatched the bee IS the Q33N that reviews its output. Do not wait for a separate session.

 Step 8: Backfill freed slots.
 - When a bee completes (pass or fail), its slot is free.
 - If there are remaining undispatched tasks, dispatch the next one immediately.
 - If a fix task was generated, it takes priority over new tasks.
 - Continue until all tasks are dispatched AND all responses are reviewed.

 Step 9: Report to Q33NR.
 - Only after ALL bees have completed and ALL responses are reviewed.
 - Write a single completion report covering the entire batch.
 - Report to Q33NR with: tasks completed, tasks failed, fix tasks dispatched, total tests, any issues.

 Step 10: Archive.
 - (Same as current Step 8 — archive + inventory CLI.)

 2. Update P-03 in PROCESS-LIBRARY-V2.md

 File: .deia/processes/PROCESS-LIBRARY-V2.md (lines 30-47)

 Add these rules to P-03 (Bee Dispatch Standard):

 Slot Management:
 - FILL ALL AVAILABLE SLOTS. If 5 slots are open and 8 independent tasks exist, dispatch 5 immediately.
 - When a slot frees (bee completes), backfill immediately with the next pending task.
 - Fix tasks take priority over new tasks when backfilling.
 - Do not exit until all dispatched bees have been reviewed.

 Monitoring Cadence:
 - After dispatching, poll `.deia/hive/responses/` every 60 seconds for new response files.
 - Match response files to dispatched task IDs (pattern: `YYYYMMDD-TASK-XXX-RESPONSE.md`).
 - Do not spin (no sub-second polling). Do not over-sleep (no 5+ minute gaps).
 - The dispatching Q33N reviews each response inline — do not defer to a separate session.

 3. Verify queue runner alignment

 File: .deia/hive/scripts/queue/run_queue.py

 The queue runner ALREADY implements all of this correctly:
 - ThreadPoolExecutor with FIRST_COMPLETED for non-spinning monitoring
 - Immediate backfill when slots clear
 - Fix specs prepended to queue (priority over new specs)
 - Hot-reload to detect new specs

 No code changes needed in run_queue.py. The queue runner is the reference implementation. The doc changes bring Q33N's
  manual workflow in line with what the queue runner already does automatically.

 4. Add cross-reference in P-14 (Queue Runner Operations)

 File: .deia/processes/PROCESS-LIBRARY-V2.md (P-14 section)

 Add a note at the top of P-14:

 The queue runner implements the same lifecycle as Q33N manual dispatch (HIVE.md Steps 6-10):
 fill slots → monitor → review → backfill → report. Q33N manual dispatch follows the same
 rules. See P-03 for shared slot management and monitoring rules.

 ────────────────────────────────────────
 File: .deia/processes/PROCESS-LIBRARY-V2.md
 Change: Add slot management + monitoring cadence rules to P-03. Add cross-reference in P-14.

 3. Cross-reference P-14 note confirms alignment
 4. Next Q33N dispatch should follow the new rules (dispatch all slots, stay alive, review inline, backfill, single
 completion report)

> only 24 tasks in 16 hours????

● You're right — that's slow. 15 actually delivered code, 4 were just Q33N writing task files (coordination overhead),
  and 5 never even got dispatched. The bees that ran completed clean, but the pipeline throughput is the problem.

  The bottlenecks I can see:

  1. Q33NR → Q33N → review → approve → dispatch is too many serial handoffs before a single bee even starts
  2. 5 tasks never started — task files sat there with nobody dispatching them
  3. Coordination-only tasks (231, 240, 241) — Q33N wrote task files and stopped, waiting for approval that never came
  because nobody was watching
  4. Single-threaded dispatch — bees ran one or two at a time instead of 5 parallel

  For a 16-hour window with parallel dispatch, this should have been 40-60 completed tasks, not 15.

  What do you want to do about it? Options:

  - Blast the undispatched backlog now — I can send Q33N to dispatch all 9 waiting tasks in parallel immediately
  - Tighten the pipeline — give Q33N standing approval to dispatch without waiting for Q33NR review (faster but less
  oversight)
  - Both — blast now + change the process for future runs

> 1 that bottlenext is NECESSARY to prevent errors in delivery. if a damn Claude Agent could actually get shit
  right the first time, we wouldnt need it.

● Fair point. The audit just proved it — two Haiku bees skipped the mandatory 8-section response file, one blew past the
   500-line limit. Without the review chain those errors ship unchecked. The pipeline isn't the problem.

  The real throughput loss is:
  - 5 tasks sitting there never dispatched — nobody was watching
  - Gaps between dispatch cycles — bee finishes, response sits for hours before Q33N picks it up
  - Q33N stopping to wait instead of dispatching everything it has approval for in parallel

  The chain of command is right. The cadence is wrong. Want me to blast the 9 undispatched tasks out now?

> no blasting until we address what you mentioned. whose role is it to make sure things get dispatched? how can we

● Searched for 1 pattern, read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

● Here's what I found:

  What IS documented:
  - P-03 says "Parallel when tasks are independent. Sequential when dependent." and HIVE.md Step 6 says "Never more than
   5 bees in parallel"
  - P-14 has the queue runner with --watch mode and Fibonacci backoff polling
  - Bee watchdog handles stale bees (8-min timeout, auto-restart)

  What is NOT documented — the gaps:

  1. No dispatch cadence rule for Q33N. HIVE.md Step 6 says "dispatch bees" but nothing about what Q33N does after
  dispatching. It just... stops. There's no rule saying "monitor running bees and dispatch the next batch as slots free
  up."
  2. No completion pickup rule. When a bee finishes and writes a response file, there's no documented trigger for Q33N
  to pick it up. Right now it requires Q33NR to manually dispatch another Q33N session to review results. That's the
  hours-long gap.
  3. Parallel dispatch is mentioned but not enforced. "Parallel when independent" is soft language. There's no rule
  saying "ALWAYS fill all 5 slots. If you have 8 independent tasks and 5 slots, dispatch 5 immediately, then backfill as
   slots clear."
  4. No standing orders for Q33N between dispatch cycles. Q33N is fire-and-forget — it runs, does one thing, exits.
  There's no "stay alive and manage the full batch lifecycle" instruction.

  So the answer is: the rules exist in pieces but nobody wrote the glue. The queue runner (run_queue.py --watch) was
  built to solve this for automated dispatch, but Q33N's manual coordination workflow has no equivalent.

  Want me to draft process updates to close these gaps?

● There's the bug. The dependency string parsed from TASK-224 is:

  TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist)

  And _deps_satisfied checks dep in done_name — so it's looking for the entire string TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol
  must exist) as a substring in 2026-03-16-SPEC-TASK-222-pipeline-store-protocol. That will never match because of the
  parenthetical comment.

  Same for TASK-242 — dep string is TASK-241 (production URLs must be verified first).

  The parser needs to strip the parenthetical. Quick fix:

> are their dependencies even in queue??

● Read 3 files (ctrl+o to expand)

● Yes, the chain is correct and they're all in queue:

  - TASK-224 (directory state machine) — just dispatched to slot 2
  - TASK-225 (inmemory pipeline store) — just dispatched to slot 3
  - TASK-226 — blocked on 224 + 225 (both now running, will unblock when they finish)
  - TASK-227 — blocked on 224 (running, will unblock when it finishes)
  - TASK-228 — blocked on 226 + 225 (226 is itself blocked on 224+225)

  It's a legit dependency chain: 222 → 224+225 → 226+227 → 228. TASK-222 is done, 224 and 225 are now running, and the
  rest will cascade-unblock as each finishes. The queue runner handles this — when a slot frees and a bee completes, it
  re-checks _done/ and unblocks the next layer.

● Searched for 1 pattern, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● There's the bug. The dependency string parsed from TASK-224 is:

  TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist)

  And _deps_satisfied checks dep in done_name — so it's looking for the
  entire string TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist) as a
  substring in 2026-03-16-SPEC-TASK-222-pipeline-store-protocol. That
  will never match because of the parenthetical comment.

  Same for TASK-242 — dep string is TASK-241 (production URLs must be
  verified first).

  The parser needs to strip the parenthetical. Quick fix:

● Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Update(.deia\hive\scripts\queue\spec_parser.py)
  ⎿  Added 3 lines
      123              line = line.strip()
      124              if line.startswith('- '):

          +222 (reason)" → "TASK-222"
      127 +                if '(' in dep_id:
      128 +                    dep_id = dep_id[:dep_id.index('(')
          +].strip()
      129                  if dep_id:
      130                      depends_on.append(dep_id)

│ Context                                                                                                                                          │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ The audit revealed that only 15 tasks completed in 16 hours because:                                                                             │
│ - Q33N dispatches bees and then exits. Nobody monitors completion.                                                                               │
│ - A separate Q33N session has to be spun up later to review results — hours-long gaps.                                                           │
│ - Parallel slots aren't being maximized.                                                                                                         │

│                                                                                                                                                  │

● There's the bug. The dependency string parsed from TASK-224 is:

  TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist)

  And _deps_satisfied checks dep in done_name — so it's looking for the entire string TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist) as a substring in
   2026-03-16-SPEC-TASK-222-pipeline-store-protocol. That will never match because of the parenthetical comment.

  Same for TASK-242 — dep string is TASK-241 (production URLs must be verified first).

  The parser needs to strip the parenthetical. Quick fix:

● Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

      123              line = line.strip()
      124              if line.startswith('- '):
      125                  dep_id = line[2:].strip()
      126 +                # Strip parenthetical comments: "TASK-222 (reason)" → "TASK-222"
      127 +                if '(' in dep_id:
      128 +                    dep_id = dep_id[:dep_id.index('(')].strip()
      129                  if dep_id:
      130                      depends_on.append(dep_id)

 Plan: Q33NR Session Logging Rule

 Context

 Q33NR sessions with Q88N used to be logged but the rule got lost. Dave wants full transcripts of every Q33NR ↔ Q88N conversation recorded to a
 file. No summarization, no token optimization — just record everything raw. Optimization can happen later if needed.

 Change

 Add session logging rule to HIVE.md under Q33NR Workflow

 File: .deia/HIVE.md — add new section after "Q33NR After Compaction (Recovery)" (after line 101), before the --- separator.

 Add:

 ### Q33NR Session Logging

 Every Q33NR session MUST be logged. Write the full transcript to:

   `.deia/hive/session-logs/YYYY-MM-DD-HHMM-Q33NR-SESSION.md`

 Log everything:
 - Every Q88N prompt (verbatim)
 - Every Q33NR response (verbatim)
 - Tool calls and bash commands: summarize as one-line descriptions (e.g. "Ran browser tests — 42 passed")
 - Tool output: omit raw output, keep the result summary

 Start the log at session start. Append as you go. If the session crashes or compacts, resume logging in the same file.

 Format:
   **Q88N:** [prompt]
   **Q33NR:** [response]
   **[action]** [one-line summary of tool/bash call and result]

 Create the session-logs directory

 Create .deia/hive/session-logs/ (empty, with a .gitkeep).

│ Step 6: Dispatch bees (fill all slots).                                                                                                          │
│ - Dispatch ALL independent tasks in parallel up to the slot limit (5 peak / 10 off-peak per queue.yml).                                          │
│ - Do not dispatch 1 or 2 when you have 8 independent tasks and 5 open slots. Fill every slot.                                                    │
│ - Dependent tasks queue behind their blockers.                                                                                                   │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Step 7: Monitor and review (stay alive).                                                                                                         │
│ - After dispatching, DO NOT EXIT. Stay alive and poll for completion.                                                                            │
│ - Check .deia/hive/responses/ for new response files matching your dispatched task IDs.                                                          │
│ - Poll every 60 seconds. Do not spin (no sub-second loops). Do not sleep for minutes.                                                            │
│ - When a response file appears, immediately review it:                                                                                           │
│   - All 8 sections present? Tests pass? No stubs? No regressions?                                                                                │
│   - If PASS: mark task as verified, write to completion report.                                                                                  │
│   - If FAIL: write a fix task and dispatch it into the freed slot (backfill).                                                                    │
│ - The Q33N that dispatched the bee IS the Q33N that reviews its output. Do not wait for a separate session.                                      │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Step 8: Backfill freed slots.                                                                                                                    │
│ - When a bee completes (pass or fail), its slot is free.                                                                                         │
│ - If there are remaining undispatched tasks, dispatch the next one immediately.                                                                  │
│ - If a fix task was generated, it takes priority over new tasks.                                                                                 │
│ - Continue until all tasks are dispatched AND all responses are reviewed.                                                                        │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Step 9: Report to Q33NR.                                                                                                                         │

  And _deps_satisfied checks dep in done_name — so it's looking for the entire string TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist) as a substring in
   2026-03-16-SPEC-TASK-222-pipeline-store-protocol. That will never match because of the parenthetical comment.

  Same for TASK-242 — dep string is TASK-241 (production URLs must be verified first).

  The parser needs to strip the parenthetical. Quick fix:

      123              line = line.strip()

      129                  if dep_id:
      130                      depends_on.append(dep_id)

 Plan: Q33NR Session Logging Rule

 Context

 Q33NR sessions with Q88N used to be logged but the rule got lost. Dave wants full transcripts of every Q33NR ↔ Q88N conversation recorded to a
 file. No summarization, no token optimization — just record everything raw. Optimization can happen later if needed.

 Change

 Add session logging rule to HIVE.md under Q33NR Workflow

 File: .deia/HIVE.md — add new section after "Q33NR After Compaction (Recovery)" (after line 101), before the --- separator.

 Add:

 ### Q33NR Session Logging

 Every Q33NR session MUST be logged. Write the full transcript to:

   `.deia/hive/session-logs/YYYY-MM-DD-HHMM-Q33NR-SESSION.md`

 Log everything:
 - Every Q88N prompt (verbatim)
 - Every Q33NR response (verbatim)
 - Tool calls and bash commands: summarize as one-line descriptions (e.g. "Ran browser tests — 42 passed")
 - Tool output: omit raw output, keep the result summary

 Start the log at session start. Append as you go. If the session crashes or compacts, resume logging in the same file.

 Format:
   **Q88N:** [prompt]
   **Q33NR:** [response]
   **[action]** [one-line summary of tool/bash call and result]

 Create the session-logs directory

 Create .deia/hive/session-logs/ (empty, with a .gitkeep).

│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ File: .deia/HIVE.md (lines 174-202)                                                                                                              │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Replace the current Steps 6-8 with a new lifecycle that covers:                                                                                  │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Step 6: Dispatch bees (fill all slots).                                                                                                          │
│ - Dispatch ALL independent tasks in parallel up to the slot limit (5 peak / 10 off-peak per queue.yml).                                          │
│ - Do not dispatch 1 or 2 when you have 8 independent tasks and 5 open slots. Fill every slot.                                                    │
│ - Dependent tasks queue behind their blockers.                                                                                                   │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Step 7: Monitor and review (stay alive).                                                                                                         │
│ - After dispatching, DO NOT EXIT. Stay alive and poll for completion.                                                                            │
│ - Check .deia/hive/responses/ for new response files matching your dispatched task IDs.                                                          │
│ - Poll every 60 seconds. Do not spin (no sub-second loops). Do not sleep for minutes.                                                            │
│ - When a response file appears, immediately review it:                                                                                           │
│   - All 8 sections present? Tests pass? No stubs? No regressions?                                                                                │
│   - If PASS: mark task as verified, write to completion report.                                                                                  │
│   - If FAIL: write a fix task and dispatch it into the freed slot (backfill).                                                                    │
│ - The Q33N that dispatched the bee IS the Q33N that reviews its output. Do not wait for a separate session.                                      │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Step 8: Backfill freed slots.                                                                                                                    │
│ - When a bee completes (pass or fail), its slot is free.                                                                                         │
│ - If there are remaining undispatched tasks, dispatch the next one immediately.                                                                  │
│ - If a fix task was generated, it takes priority over new tasks.                                                                                 │
│ - Continue until all tasks are dispatched AND all responses are reviewed.                                                                        │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Step 9: Report to Q33NR.                                                                                                                         │
│ - Only after ALL bees have completed and ALL responses are reviewed.                                                                             │
│ - Write a single completion report covering the entire batch.                                                                                    │
│ - Report to Q33NR with: tasks completed, tasks failed, fix tasks dispatched, total tests, any issues.                                            │
│                                                                                                                                                  │
│ Step 10: Archive.                                                                                                                                │

  TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist)

  And _deps_satisfied checks dep in done_name — so it's looking for the entire string TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist) as a substring in
   2026-03-16-SPEC-TASK-222-pipeline-store-protocol. That will never match because of the parenthetical comment.

  Same for TASK-242 — dep string is TASK-241 (production URLs must be verified first).

  The parser needs to strip the parenthetical. Quick fix:

      123              line = line.strip()

● Searched for 1 pattern, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● There's the bug. The dependency string parsed from TASK-224 is:

  TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist)

  And _deps_satisfied checks dep in done_name — so it's looking for the entire string TASK-222 (PipelineStore protocol must exist) as a substring in
   2026-03-16-SPEC-TASK-222-pipeline-store-protocol. That will never match because of the parenthetical comment.

  Same for TASK-242 — dep string is TASK-241 (production URLs must be verified first).

  The parser needs to strip the parenthetical. Quick fix:

● Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

● Update(.deia\hive\scripts\queue\spec_parser.py)
  ⎿  Added 3 lines
      123              line = line.strip()
      124              if line.startswith('- '):
      125                  dep_id = line[2:].strip()
      126 +                # Strip parenthetical comments: "TASK-222 (reason)" → "TASK-222"
      127 +                if '(' in dep_id:
      128 +                    dep_id = dep_id[:dep_id.index('(')].strip()
      129                  if dep_id:
      130                      depends_on.append(dep_id)
      131
